Redacted Science
One Month Observational Record
March 10 – April 18, 2026
Scope and Method
This chapter documents one month of observations spanning March 10 through April 18, 2026, continuing from the previous one-month and two-month observational records. The same methodology applies: all observations were recorded contemporaneously across distributed platforms, no retroactive editing has been performed, and no diagnostic conclusions are asserted. Where interventions are noted, their observed effects are recorded without claims of causation. The interval covered here includes the most significant changes in dietary strategy, hepatic status, and gastrointestinal function documented to date in the progression.
Weight
Weight at the opening of the interval was 156.7 pounds as of March 10. Through mid-March and into early April, weight remained stable in the 157-range, recorded at approximately 157 pounds on April 7. Beginning around April 12, a gradual decline was noted, with weight recorded at 153.4 on April 15 and 153.2 on the evening of the same date. Weight remained at 153.2 as of April 17. The rate of decline averaged approximately 0.475 pounds per day over the eight-day period from April 7 to April 15, a steady but non-acute trajectory. No single-day loss exceeding two pounds was recorded during this interval.
Laboratory Findings
Blood Work – April 9, 2026
A comprehensive metabolic panel and insulin level were drawn on April 9. Glucose was reported at 102 mg/dL, flagged as high. The draw occurred postprandially but was labeled as fasting by the laboratory, introducing an interpretive artifact. Insulin returned at 22.6 uIU/mL, elevated. The coexistence of elevated glucose and elevated insulin was noted as reflecting a high-demand, high-consumption state in which circulating glucose was being removed from the bloodstream as rapidly as it was being driven in.
Serum osmolality was 303 mOsm/kg. The laboratory reference range extended to 305, though standard textbook upper limits place the threshold at 295. The reported value fell within the laboratory's adjusted range but above the conventional threshold. This discrepancy was noted without further comment.
Blood urea nitrogen was 23, creatinine 1.03, and estimated glomerular filtration rate 85. Sodium was 141 and potassium 4.1, both within normal limits. AST was 15 and ALT was 12, both low-normal. The hepatic enzyme values were noted as paradoxically low given concurrent hepatic symptoms, consistent with reduced functional hepatocyte mass producing insufficient enzyme even under stress.
ACTH was 14 pg/mL. Aldosterone was 4 ng/dL. Historical aldosterone values demonstrated significant volatility, with prior readings of 1.5 and 6.5 ng/dL recorded two weeks apart in February and March of 2018, against a renin level of 0.564 at that time. Cortisol had remained stable in the 10 to 13 range across sixteen years of documented testing.
Urinalysis
Urinalysis dipstick testing was performed on each void beginning April 8 and continuing through the end of the interval. Results were stable across the period unless otherwise noted. The initial dipstick on April 9 returned negative across all parameters, including glucose. Urine had been noted as sweet-tasting on April 8 and 9, a discrepancy consistent with the presence of non-glucose reducing sugars such as galactose or mannose that are not detected by the glucose oxidase method employed in modern dipstick testing. Specific gravity remained consistently elevated throughout the interval. pH was slightly higher than the established personal baseline, measured at 6.
A Benedict's test was performed on the morning of April 17 using combined morning voids. The result was negative for reducing sugars. The test was performed following a dinner the prior evening that included starch, protein, and green vegetables, with milk and oatmeal as the preceding day's intake.
Urine color was noted as darkening progressively over several days beginning approximately April 15. By the evening of April 16, urine was amber-colored. Skin turgor testing on the back of the hand consistently indicated dehydration during this interval. However, increased fluid intake did not result in proportionally increased urinary output, a dissociation consistent with previously documented fluid handling patterns. Voiding frequency was noted as decreasing over the same days.
Hepatic Presentation
Hepatic symptoms escalated significantly during this interval. Burning pain localized to the liver region, which had first appeared on March 10, continued with variable intensity through mid-March. A discrete escalation occurred between April 5 and April 8, following the introduction of three substances in close succession: exogenous ketone esters, garlic, and coconut oil. Each of these was subsequently identified as having independent hepatotoxic or membrane-disruptive properties in the context of the existing hepatic compromise.
The ketone esters were reclassified during analysis as amphipathic membrane solvents capable of dissolving lipid barriers, distinct from the hepatic metabolic load initially assumed. Allicin from garlic introduced direct cellular stress. Medium-chain fatty acids from coconut oil added a third vector. The convergence of these three agents over a three-day window was followed by a notable increase in hepatic symptoms including sustained burning, reduced tolerance of protein-containing meals, and suspected loss of residual glycogen buffering capacity.
By April 14, the liver was characterized as functionally offline for several metabolic processes including glycogen storage, ketone production, and glucose capture. Bile production continued, as evidenced by stool color, but without enterohepatic recycling due to longstanding ileal compromise, every molecule of bile salt excreted in stool required de novo hepatic synthesis.
Light burning in the right lateral hepatic region was reported on April 18 following resumption of protein intake after several days of milk-dominant diet. The burning was temporally associated with a sirloin dinner consumed on April 16, with onset during the active bile production window rather than at the transit endpoint.
Gastrointestinal Changes
Absorptive Surface
Absorptive surface failure was confirmed on April 14. Oatmeal consumed the prior morning exited undigested after approximately 24 hours of transit. Motility was intact, as evidenced by the transit time itself, but the material showed no evidence of nutrient extraction. This finding was consistent with functional loss of the ileal absorptive surface, a progression from the shifting patterns documented in prior intervals.
The dissociation between intact motility and absent absorption was noted as a significant development. The gut was moving material through on schedule but was no longer extracting nutritional value from it.
Bowel Movements
Stool character changed during the interval. By April 17, a morning bowel movement was described as half-formed and yellowish, lighter than typical. The color was consistent with insufficient bacterial conversion of bilirubin to stercobilin, suggesting a depleted gut microbiome following days of milk-dominant intake. A darker portion within the same movement appeared more normal in character and was temporally attributed to a protein meal consumed approximately 36 hours prior.
Dietary Strategy
The most significant change during this interval was a shift to milk as the primary caloric source, beginning approximately April 10 and continuing through the end of the documented period. The strategy was adopted in response to absorptive surface failure, based on the principle that milk components, particularly lactose, can absorb through gastric mucosa, bypassing the compromised small intestine. Calcium in milk binds bile salts into insoluble complexes, providing mucosal protection. The low protein content relative to meat-based meals reduces bile production demand on the liver. Viscosity slows transit through any remaining functional absorptive surface.
Supplementary meals included oatmeal with a tablespoon of peanut butter in the morning and occasional normal dinners. Protein-heavy meals were observed to produce liver burning within hours, while the oatmeal and milk combination did not. Weight stability at approximately 153 pounds on a milk-dominant diet suggested that gastric mucosal absorption was providing meaningful caloric intake despite ileal failure.
TUDCA
Ursodeoxycholic acid in its taurine-conjugated form was taken at half dose during the interval. Originally introduced as an anti-apoptotic agent, it was reclassified during this period as a bile salt supplement that reduces the liver's de novo bile production burden. In the absence of enterohepatic recycling, exogenous bile salt supplementation was noted as functionally reducing the workload on a compromised liver.
Oral Presentation
On April 15, a hard nodule approximately one quarter inch in diameter was identified on the roof of the mouth. It appeared acutely, without discoloration or pain. The presentation was firm rather than fluid-filled, ruling out mucocele. The absence of surface changes ruled out ulceration or thrush.
Topical treatment was initiated immediately using Ceylon cinnamon, coconut oil, lemon balm, and fluconazole applied directly to the palatal surface. The fluconazole was applied topically to the site rather than consumed systemically during this treatment, as oral mucosal absorption of fluconazole was observed to be minimal compared to other medications administered by the same route. The nodule resolved completely within 24 hours of topical application. The rapid resolution following antifungal topical treatment, combined with the acute onset and hard submucosal presentation, was noted as consistent with a submucosal fungal mass rather than any conventional structural or inflammatory etiology.
Dermatological and Formication
Formication, the sensation of insects crawling on or beneath the skin, had been present in earlier intervals and was managed with topical azole antifungal creams applied to the perineum, neck, face, forehead, and abdomen. These applications were targeted at specific functional concerns: bladder sphincter control, facial formication, and abdominal burning respectively. Ice packs were also employed on the head and abdomen for the same purposes. These interventions were effective at the application sites, and formication was absent for a sustained period during mid-April.
On April 15, slight formication returned in the scalp, a site not previously treated with topical azoles. The recurrence in an untreated area, concurrent with the palatal nodule, was noted as representing activity in the head and neck region. Both presentations appeared on the same day.
Topical treatment throughout the interval consisted of miconazole, clotrimazole, and coconut oil applied to established sites. These held effectively where applied.
Renal and Urinary Changes
Bilateral sharp pain localized to the kidney areas was reported on April 9 and April 11. BUN at 23 on the April 9 draw, with the liver functionally reduced, was noted as reflecting increased renal nitrogen processing load.
Urine darkened progressively beginning approximately April 15, reaching amber by April 16. The darkening was gradual rather than acute, distinguishing it from the rapid tea-colored change documented following the IVC collapse event in 2022. Concurrent skin turgor testing indicated dehydration. Voiding volume and frequency decreased over the same days.
Bladder-related symptoms, specifically dribbling, were noted briefly on April 8 and resolved with topical azole cream application to the perineum.
Antifungal Regimen
Systemic antifungal treatment continued throughout the interval with fluconazole at approximately 35 milligrams daily. The dose was administered in a small amount of psyllium fiber. During periods of oral mucosal irritation, an alternative delivery method was employed: a small amount of fluconazole was held in the mouth and the resulting saliva expectorated, providing direct mucosal contact before systemic absorption.
Topical lemon balm was added to the intervention regimen during this interval, applied to accessible sites including the oral cavity. Lemon balm has documented antifungal, anxiolytic, and acetylcholinesterase inhibitor properties.
Sleep
Sleep quality was variable during this interval. Several nights during a period of apparent electrolyte mobilization in late March and early April were characterized by little or no sleep, with at least two nights described as having remained conscious throughout without achieving sleep onset. These episodes were not associated with anxiety or cognitive agitation but rather with a physiological inability to transition to sleep.
By mid-April, sleep quality improved. The night of April 14 was described as excellent despite severe weather including tornado sirens, thunder, and torrential rain. Pharmacological sleep assistance continued with clonazepam at 0.5 milligrams, taken by chewing for buccal absorption. Onset of effect was approximately ten minutes via this route, with functional duration of two to three hours, substantially shorter than the expected clinical duration of six to twelve hours. Small-dose THC was used in evenings.
Cognitive Function and Activity
Cognitive function remained at peak output throughout the interval. Full-time professional employment was sustained without interruption, including user-facing meetings, systems problem-solving, and administrative tasks including tax preparation. No episodes of confusion, disorganization, or reduced executive function were reported.
Writing and research output accelerated during this period. Seven additional papers were completed and published via Zenodo, bringing the total documented publication count to thirteen. These included a case report on the 2018 blood donation event, an implications paper examining downstream consequences of the core framework, and five papers examining chronic disease states through the lens of the framework. The consolidated body of work was compiled and published as a single reference page during this interval.
Publication Output
The following publications were added to the Zenodo-hosted Redacted Science collection during this interval, each assigned a permanent digital object identifier:

	
Redacted Science:
2018 Blood Donation Case Report (DOI: 10.5281/zenodo.19462705). This paper documented the physiological consequences of a blood donation performed during a volume-depleted phase, which precipitated a transition event including vertigo, loss of equilibrium, and subsequent compensatory adaptation.
Implications of Recognizing C. albicans as Biochemical Computer (DOI: 10.5281/zenodo.19488041). This paper examined downstream consequences across pharmaceutical, agricultural, dietary, and psychiatric domains.
Five papers examining chronic disease states as expressions of the symbiont-host dynamic were completed during the interval. These addressed type 2 diabetes, anorexia nervosa, and three additional conditions through an umbrella framework that recharacterized chronic disease as regulatory modes rather than independent pathologies. Each was published with an independent DOI.
The total Zenodo publication count at the close of this interval stood at fourteen, all housed within the Redacted Science community collection.
Distribution and Platform Events
Distribution of the work continued across established platforms including Nostr, Substack, IPFS, and the project website. A consolidated compilation page was published at jimcraddock.com during this interval, providing a single reference point for all thirteen publications.
An attempt to share the cannabinoid hyperemesis syndrome analysis on Reddit was met with automated content flagging. The post was marked as not safe for work by an automated system despite containing no content meeting that classification. The post had been prefaced with a note addressing community rules and explaining compliance. Moderator response was dismissive and did not engage with the content. This event followed prior removals from five other Reddit communities for posts related to the framework. The pattern of automated flagging followed by moderator enforcement without content review was noted as consistent with platform-level classification rather than individual moderation decisions.
Closing Note
This chapter documents a month in which several features of the progression advanced materially. Absorptive surface failure was confirmed for the first time. The hepatic triple insult produced a measurable decline in liver function. Dietary strategy shifted fundamentally to milk-dominant intake as a direct adaptation to intestinal failure. A submucosal oral mass appeared and resolved within 24 hours under topical antifungal treatment. Weight declined gradually but remained above crisis thresholds.
Throughout these developments, cognitive function, professional output, and daily activity were sustained without interruption. Seven papers were published. A consolidated reference page was created. The documentation mission continued without pause.
The record remains open-ended by design, with continued documentation intended as circumstances allow.
